2021  7:35 a.m.</time></dd></div></dl></div><div class="col-span-12 flex flex-col gap-12"><div class="flex flex-col border-t border-low-contrast pt-3 lg:border-t-0"><h3 class="type-mono-ui3 class="flex items-center gap-3 md:gap-6"><button type="button" class="inline-flex items-center gap-1 text-high-contrast hover:text-accent -m-3 p-3" aria-label="Share this content"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 0.933145 5.5907C0.977602 5.66788 1.04456 5.72966 1.12507 5.76777L5.90639 8.09417L8.2328 12.875C8.27091 12.9555 8.33269 13.0224 8.40987 13.0669C8.48706 13.1113 8.57597 13.1312 8.66473 13.1237C8.7535 13.1163 8.83787 13.082 8.90659 13.0253C8.97531 12.9686 9.02509 12.8923 9.04929 12.8066L12.2332 2.30714Z" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="1.25" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path></g></svg></button></div></div><div id="page-content" class="relative space-y-article-blocks mt-8 min-h-full w-full gap-y-site-grid-gutter md:mt-16"><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span><em>Julia Schuetze is the Jr Project Director for International Cybersecurity Policy at Stiftung Neue Verantwortung e.V.&nbsp;</em><em>Arthur de Liedekerke is a cybersecurity analyst with prior experience in the European Union institutions.&nbsp;</em><em>The views and opinions expressed in this article are solely those of the authors and do not reflect the official position or policy of their employers.</em></span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>On April 15, the same day that the United States <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/statements-releases/2021/04/15/fact-sheet-imposing-costs-for-harmful-foreign-activities-by-the-russian-government/" target="_blank" title="imposed">imposed</a> sanctions against Russia for the SolarWinds cyber espionage campaign, election interference, and other issues, the European Union (EU) <a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2021/04/15/declaration-by-the-high-representative-on-behalf-of-the-european-union-expressing-solidarity-with-the-united-states-on-the-impact-of-the-solarwinds-cyber-operation/" target="_blank" title="published">published</a> a declaration expressing solidarity with the United States. A month later, on May 14, the European Council <a href="https://protect-us.mimecast.com/s/rEbtCmZMqQS5PKWouGYoUB?domain=consilium.europa.eu/" target="_blank" title="extended">extended</a> the sanctions regime that guides response to cyber attacks that threaten the EU or its members until May 2022. As part of the EU’s cyber diplomacy toolbox, a declaration falls into <a href="https://data.consilium.europa.eu/doc/document/ST-13007-2017-INIT/en/pdf" target="_blank" title="category three">category three</a> [PDF] of responses—stability measures—which express concern or condemn general cyber trends or certain cyber activities and could have a signaling function. While the EU’s issuance of the declaration in response to SolarWinds is a sign of progress, it fails to provide clarification on what, if any, further actions can be expected from Brussels.</span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>The declaration still matters because it shows that the EU’s response process to malicious cyber activities is maturing. This declaration differs from previous responses due to its coordinated timing with the imposition of U.S. sanctions and reference to Washington’s attribution of the campaign to Russia. This contrasts with previous EU responses where <a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2018/04/16/malicious-cyber-activities-council-adopts-conclusions/" target="_blank" title="attribution was not mentioned explicitly">attribution was not mentioned explicitly</a> or where member states independently <a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/blaming-russia-for-notpetya-was-coordinated-diplomatic-action/" target="_blank" title="coordinated their attribution efforts multilaterally">coordinated their attribution efforts multilaterally</a> with third states, avoiding attribution through a unified <a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2018/04/16/malicious-cyber-activities-council-adopts-conclusions/" target="_blank" title="EU-wide response">EU-wide response</a>.</span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>Additionally, the language of the EU’s recent declaration deviates from prior statements, like those responding to <a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2020/02/21/declaration-by-the-high-representative-on-behalf-of-the-european-union-call-to-promote-and-conduct-responsible-behaviour-in-cyberspace/" target="_blank" title="election interference">election interference</a> in Georgia and cyber threats <a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2020/04/30/declaration-by-the-high-representative-josep-borrell-on-behalf-of-the-european-union-on-malicious-cyber-activities-exploiting-the-coronavirus-pandemic/" target="_blank" title="targeting">targeting</a> the health-care sector during the pandemic. Instead of “condemning” the SolarWinds campaign, the declaration expressed the EU’s solidarity with the United States “<a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2021/04/15/declaration-by-the-high-representative-on-behalf-of-the-european-union-expressing-solidarity-with-the-united-states-on-the-impact-of-the-solarwinds-cyber-operation/" target="_blank" title="on the impact of malicious cyber activities">on the impact of malicious cyber activities</a><a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2021/04/15/declaration-by-the-high-representative-on-behalf-of-the-european-union-expressing-solidarity-with-the-united-states-on-the-impact-of-the-solarwinds-cyber-operation/" target="_blank" title="."><em>.</em></a>”<em> </em>Simply expressing solidarity with the impact in the United States reflects that the European Union does not per se condemn this type of activity. Moreover, it treads carefully when referring to the impact the operation had on the EU and its member states.</span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>This could have been more directly connected to where the EU explains its concern about malicious activities in general that are “affecting the security and integrity of information and communication technology (ICT) products and services, which might have systemic effects and cause significant harm to our society, security and economy.” This vague description could be an attempt to show that, from an EU standpoint, the seemingly indiscriminate nature of the SolarWinds breach (“the compromise affected governments and businesses worldwide, including in EU Member States”) and apparent disregard for collateral damage (“systemic effects with potential significant harm to our society, security and economy”) could result in consequences for the perpetrator. However, by not being more concrete on the damage the campaign had on the EU, falls short of indicating whether those behind it crossed a red line that requires a strong response from the EU. As the rest of the statement focuses on preventative efforts that the EU is already undertaking, the text does not signal that such incidents could be met with a more assertive response, such as restrictive measures. The statement also ignores the fact that two days before the Declaration came out&nbsp; technical evidence seems to suggest that the EU’s sanctions regime could be applied. In an <a href="https://www.europarl.europa.eu/doceo/document/P-9-2021-001112-ASW_EN.pdf" target="_blank" title="answer to a parliamentary question">answer to a parliamentary question</a> on April 13, European Commissioner for Budget and Administration Johannes Hahn indicated that the EU’s computer emergency response team (CERT-EU) had identified cases where IT networks and systems had been<b> “</b>significantly impacted” and personal data breaches occurred. “Significant impact” or “potentially significant effect” is one threshold <a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2019/05/17/cyber-attacks-council-is-now-able-to-impose-sanctions/" target="_blank" title="covered in the sanctions regime">covered in the sanctions regime</a>.</span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>Whether the EU will follow up <a href="https://data.consilium.europa.eu/doc/document/ST-5664-2018-INIT/en/pdf" target="_blank" title="with sanctions">with sanctions</a>—like the United States—will also likely depend on two things: the collective determination to impose costs despite the risks of retaliation, and on the outcome of further investigation mentioned in the Declaration itself vis-à-vis the other required thresholds for sanctions..</span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>Member states appear ready to act. Unofficial reports indicate that a number of <a href="https://tass.com/world/1278807" target="_blank" title="EU member states are toying with the idea of introducing sanctions">EU member states are toying with the idea of introducing sanctions</a> against Russian citizens who were allegedly involved in the SolarWinds campaign. Also, given the steady deterioration of EU-Russia relations in recent months, member states could be tempted to demonstrate their collective determination to push back against Russia and their commitment to the transatlantic alliance.</span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>With the second issue, it’s possible that sanctions have not yet been imposed by the EU because its investigation is ongoing. Historically, EU cyber sanctions have been <a href="https://www.sueddeutsche.de/politik/hack-bundestag-angriff-russland-1.4891668" target="_blank" title="imposed">imposed</a> against Russian individuals and entities only after the collection of evidence and attribution by at least two EU member states. Attribution by the United States could be insufficient on its own to warrant such a response. <a name="_tumqdi4dw05z"></a>It is also possible that the EU is taking its time to aiming to create a sanctions bundle. Like the United States, the EU has <a href="https://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/press/press-releases/2020/07/30/eu-imposes-the-first-ever-sanctions-against-cyber-attacks/" target="_blank" title="sanctioned different entities for various malicious activities at the same time.">sanctioned different entities for various malicious activities at the same time.</a></span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>The EU response process is maturing, showing steady improvement in its coordination with third countries. Still, it would have been better if the EU had explicitly described the impact the SolarWinds attack had on EU interests. Such clarity would, if Brussels does eventually follow through with a stronger response such as sanctions, signal that the attacks crossed a threshold. However, considering the time constraint of aligning with the U.S. response and the need for consensus-making in the EU, it is possible that the Declaration was only a first careful response and it will soon follow-up with stronger language and/ or other means.</span></p></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin" data-block="core/paragraph" data-block-start="core/paragraph" data-block-end="core/paragraph" data-block-align=""><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><p class="rich-text type-serif-body4"><span>&nbsp;</span></p></div></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin"><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"></div></div><div class="grid grid-cols-site grid-rows-1 gap-x-site-grid-gutter px-site-margin mt-8"><div class="lg:row-start-1 lg:row-end-1 col-span-full sm:col-span-8 lg:col-start-13 lg:col-end-25"><aside class="flex flex-col gap-y-10 border-t border-low-contrast pt-6" aria-labelledby="_R_1bav5ubslb_"><h2 class="sr-only" id="_R_1bav5ubslb_">Information</h2><p class="type-serif-h7">From<!-- --> <a class="link-underline" href="/series/net-politics">Net Politics</a> and <a class="link-underline" href="/programs/digital-and-cyberspace-policy-program">Digital and Cyberspace Policy Program</a></p><div class="flex gap-x-site-grid-gutter"><div class="mt:-1 h-fit w-1/6 max-w-5 shrink-0"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="#000000" viewBox="0 0 512 512"><g><g><path d="M438.144,75.027C388.976,25.944,325.844,0,255.577,0C186.042,0,123.872,25.687,75.781,74.292
